    15	// histogram : reads values from stdin and outputs an histogram
    16	
    17	package main
    18	
    19	import (
    20	        "bufio"
    21	        "encoding/json"
    22	        "flag"
    23	        "fmt"
    24	        "os"
    25	        "strconv"
    26	
    27	        "fortio.org/fortio/stats"
    28	        "fortio.org/log"
    29	)
    30	
    31	func main() {
    32	        var (
    33	                offsetFlag      = flag.Float64("offset", 0.0, "Offset for the data")
    34	                dividerFlag     = flag.Float64("divider", 1, "Divider/scaling for the data")
    35	                percentilesFlag = flag.String("p", "50,75,99,99.9", "List of pXX to calculate")
    36	                jsonFlag        = flag.Bool("json", false, "Json output")
    37	        )
    38	        flag.Parse()
    39	        h := stats.NewHistogram(*offsetFlag, *dividerFlag)
    40	        percList, err := stats.ParsePercentiles(*percentilesFlag)
    41	        if err != nil {
    42	                log.Fatalf("Unable to extract percentiles from -p: %v", err)
    43	        }
    44	
    45	        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(os.Stdin)
    46	        linenum := 1
    47	        for scanner.Scan() {
    48	                line := scanner.Text()
    49	                v, err := strconv.ParseFloat(line, 64)
    50	                if err != nil {
    51	                        log.Fatalf("Can't parse line %d: %v", linenum, err)
    52	                }
    53	                h.Record(v)
    54	                linenum++
    55	        }
    56	        if err := scanner.Err(); err != nil {
    57	                log.Fatalf("Err reading standard input %v", err)
    58	        }
    59	        if *jsonFlag {
    60	                b, err := json.MarshalIndent(h.Export().CalcPercentiles(percList), "", "  ")
    61	                if err != nil {
    62	                        log.Fatalf("Unable to create Json: %v", err)
    63	                }
    64	                fmt.Print(string(b))
    65	        } else {
    66	                h.Print(os.Stdout, "Histogram", percList)
    67	        }
    68	}
    69

    30	// Counter is a type whose instances record values
    31	// and calculate stats (count, average, min, max, and stddev).
    32	type Counter struct {
    33	        Count        int64
    34	        Min          float64
    35	        Max          float64
    36	        Sum          float64
    37	        sumOfSquares float64
    38	}
    39	
    40	// Record records a data point.
    41	func (c *Counter) Record(v float64) {
    42	        c.RecordN(v, 1)
    43	}
    44	
    45	// RecordN efficiently records the same value N times.
    46	func (c *Counter) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
    47	        isFirst := (c.Count == 0)
    48	        c.Count += int64(n)
    49	        switch {
    50	        case isFirst:
    51	                c.Min = v
    52	                c.Max = v
    53	        case v < c.Min:
    54	                c.Min = v
    55	        case v > c.Max:
    56	                c.Max = v
    57	        }
    58	        s := v * float64(n)
    59	        c.Sum += s
    60	        c.sumOfSquares += (s * s)
    61	}
    62	
    63	// Avg returns the average.
    64	func (c *Counter) Avg() float64 {
    65	        if c.Count == 0 {
    66	                return 0.
    67	        }
    68	        return c.Sum / float64(c.Count)
    69	}
    70	
    71	// StdDev returns the standard deviation.
    72	func (c *Counter) StdDev() float64 {
    73	        if c.Count == 0 {
    74	                return 0.
    75	        }
    76	        fC := float64(c.Count)
    77	        sigma := (c.sumOfSquares - c.Sum*c.Sum/fC) / fC
    78	        // should never happen but it does
    79	        if sigma < 0 {
    80	                log.Warnf("Unexpected negative sigma for %+v: %g", c, sigma)
    81	                return 0
    82	        }
    83	        return math.Sqrt(sigma)
    84	}
    85	
    86	// Print prints stats.
    87	func (c *Counter) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
    88	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
    89	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    90	}
    91	
    92	// Log outputs the stats to the logger.
    93	func (c *Counter) Log(msg string) {
    94	        log.Infof("%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g",
    95	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    96	}
    97	
    98	// Reset clears the counter to reset it to original 'no data' state.
    99	func (c *Counter) Reset() {
   100	        var empty Counter
   101	        *c = empty
   102	}
   103	
   104	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Counter and clears src.
   105	func (c *Counter) Transfer(src *Counter) {
   106	        if src.Count == 0 {
   107	                return // nothing to do
   108	        }
   109	        if c.Count == 0 {
   110	                *c = *src // copy everything at once
   111	                src.Reset()
   112	                return
   113	        }
   114	        c.Count += src.Count
   115	        if src.Min < c.Min {
   116	                c.Min = src.Min
   117	        }
   118	        if src.Max > c.Max {
   119	                c.Max = src.Max
   120	        }
   121	        c.Sum += src.Sum
   122	        c.sumOfSquares += src.sumOfSquares
   123	        src.Reset()
   124	}
   125	
   126	// Histogram - written in go with inspiration from https://github.com/facebook/wdt/blob/master/util/Stats.h
   127	
   128	// The intervals are [prev, current] so for "90" (previous is 80) the values in that bucket are >80 and <=90
   129	// that way a cumulative % up to that bucket means X% of the data <= 90 (or 100-X% > 90), works well for max too
   130	// There are 2 special buckets - the first one is from min to and including 0,
   131	// one after the last for value > last and up to max.
   132	var (
   133	        histogramBucketValues = []int32{
   134	                0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6,
   135	                7, 8, 9, 10, 11, // initially increment buckets by 1, my amp goes to 11 !
   136	                12, 14, 16, 18, 20, // then by 2
   137	                25, 30, 35, 40, 45, 50, // then by 5
   138	                60, 70, 80, 90, 100, // then by 10
   139	                120, 140, 160, 180, 200, // line3 *10
   140	                250, 300, 350, 400, 450, 500, // line4 *10
   141	                600, 700, 800, 900, 1000, // line5 *10
   142	                2000, 3000, 4000, 5000, 7500, 10000, // another order of magnitude coarsly covered
   143	                20000, 30000, 40000, 50000, 75000, 100000, // ditto, the end
   144	        }
   145	        numValues  = len(histogramBucketValues)
   146	        numBuckets = numValues + 1 // 1 special first bucket is <= 0; and 1 extra last bucket is > 100000
   147	        firstValue = float64(histogramBucketValues[0])
   148	        lastValue  = float64(histogramBucketValues[numValues-1])
   149	        val2Bucket []int // ends at 1000. Remaining values will not be received in constant time.
   150	
   151	        maxArrayValue      = int32(1000) // Last value looked up as O(1) array, the rest is linear search
   152	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1          // Index of maxArrayValue
   153	)
   154	
   155	// Histogram extends Counter and adds a histogram.
   156	// Must be created using NewHistogram or anotherHistogram.Clone()
   157	// and not directly.
   158	type Histogram struct {
   159	        Counter
   160	        Offset  float64 // offset applied to data before fitting into buckets
   161	        Divider float64 // divider applied to data before fitting into buckets
   162	        // Don't access directly (outside of this package):
   163	        Hdata []int32 // numValues buckets (one more than values, for last one)
   164	}
   165	
   166	// For export of the data:
   167	
   168	// Interval is a range from start to end.
   169	// Interval are left closed, open right expect the last one which includes Max.
   170	// i.e., [Start, End] with the next one being [PrevEnd, NextEnd].
   171	type Interval struct {
   172	        Start float64
   173	        End   float64
   174	}
   175	
   176	// Bucket is the data for 1 bucket: an Interval and the occurrence Count for
   177	// that interval.
   178	type Bucket struct {
   179	        Interval
   180	        Percent float64 // Cumulative percentile
   181	        Count   int64   // How many in this bucket
   182	}
   183	
   184	// Percentile value for the percentile.
   185	type Percentile struct {
   186	        Percentile float64 // For this Percentile
   187	        Value      float64 // value at that Percentile
   188	}
   189	
   190	// HistogramData is the exported Histogram data, a sorted list of intervals
   191	// covering [Min, Max]. Pure data, so Counter for instance is flattened.
   192	type HistogramData struct {
   193	        Count       int64
   194	        Min         float64
   195	        Max         float64
   196	        Sum         float64
   197	        Avg         float64
   198	        StdDev      float64
   199	        Data        []Bucket
   200	        Percentiles []Percentile `json:"Percentiles,omitempty"`
   201	}
   202	
   203	// NewHistogram creates a new histogram (sets up the buckets).
   204	// Divider value can not be zero, otherwise returns zero.
   205	func NewHistogram(offset float64, divider float64) *Histogram {
   206	        if divider == 0 {
   207	                return nil
   208	        }
   209	        h := Histogram{
   210	                Offset:  offset,
   211	                Divider: divider,
   212	                Hdata:   make([]int32, numBuckets),
   213	        }
   214	        return &h
   215	}
   216	
   217	// Val2Bucket values are kept in two different structure
   218	// val2Bucket allows you reach between 0 and 1000 in constant time.
   219	//
   220	//nolint:gochecknoinits // we need to init these.
   221	func init() {
   222	        val2Bucket = make([]int, maxArrayValue)
   223	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1
   224	        for i, value := range histogramBucketValues {
   225	                if value == maxArrayValue {
   226	                        maxArrayValueIndex = i
   227	                        break
   228	                }
   229	        }
   230	        if maxArrayValueIndex == -1 {
   231	                log.Fatalf("Bug boundary maxArrayValue=%d not found in bucket list %v", maxArrayValue, histogramBucketValues)
   232	        }
   233	        idx := 0
   234	        for i := range maxArrayValue {
   235	                if i >= histogramBucketValues[idx] {
   236	                        idx++
   237	                }
   238	                val2Bucket[i] = idx
   239	        }
   240	        // coding bug detection (aka impossible if it works once) until 1000
   241	        if idx != maxArrayValueIndex {
   242	                log.Fatalf("Bug in creating histogram index idx %d vs index %d up to %d", idx, int(maxArrayValue), maxArrayValue)
   243	        }
   244	}
   245	
   246	// lookUpIdx looks for scaledValue's index in histogramBucketValues
   247	// TODO: change linear time to O(log(N)) with binary search.
   248	func lookUpIdx(scaledValue int) int {
   249	        scaledValue32 := int32(scaledValue) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   250	        if scaledValue32 < maxArrayValue {  // constant
   251	                return val2Bucket[scaledValue]
   252	        }
   253	        for i := maxArrayValueIndex; i < numValues; i++ {
   254	                if histogramBucketValues[i] > scaledValue32 {
   255	                        return i
   256	                }
   257	        }
   258	        log.Fatalf("never reached/bug")
   259	        return 0
   260	}
   261	
   262	// Record records a data point.
   263	func (h *Histogram) Record(v float64) {
   264	        h.RecordN(v, 1)
   265	}
   266	
   267	// RecordN efficiently records a data point N times.
   268	func (h *Histogram) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
   269	        h.Counter.RecordN(v, n)
   270	        h.record(v, n)
   271	}
   272	
   273	// Records v value to count times.
   274	func (h *Histogram) record(v float64, count int) {
   275	        // Scaled value to bucketize - we used to subtract epsilon because the interval
   276	        // is open to the left ] start, end ] so when exactly on start it has
   277	        // to fall on the previous bucket: which is more correctly done using
   278	        // math.Ceil()-1 but that doesn't work... so back to epsilon distance.
   279	        scaledVal := (v - h.Offset) / h.Divider
   280	        var idx int
   281	        switch {
   282	        case scaledVal <= firstValue:
   283	                idx = 0
   284	        case scaledVal > lastValue:
   285	                idx = numBuckets - 1 // last bucket is for > last value
   286	        default:
   287	                // else we look it up (with the open interval adjustment)
   288	                svInt := int(scaledVal)
   289	                delta := scaledVal - float64(svInt)
   290	                if delta < 1e-12 {
   291	                        svInt--
   292	                }
   293	                log.Debugf("v %f -> scaledVal %.17f ceil %f delta %g - svInt %d", v, scaledVal, math.Ceil(scaledVal), delta, svInt)
   294	                idx = lookUpIdx(svInt)
   295	        }
   296	        h.Hdata[idx] += int32(count) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   297	}
   298	
   299	// CalcPercentile returns the value for an input percentile
   300	// e.g., for 90. as input returns an estimate of the original value threshold
   301	// where 90.0% of the data is below said threshold.
   302	// with 3 data points 10, 20, 30; p0-p33.33 == 10, p 66.666 = 20, p100 = 30
   303	// p33.333 - p66.666 = linear between 10 and 20; so p50 = 15
   304	// TODO: consider spreading the count of the bucket evenly from start to end
   305	// so the % grows by at least to 1/N on start of range, and for last range
   306	// when start == end we should get to that % faster.
   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached
   328	}
   329	
   330	// Export translate the internal representation of the histogram data in
   331	// an externally usable one. Calculates the request Percentiles.
   332	func (h *Histogram) Export() *HistogramData {
   333	        var res HistogramData
   334	        res.Count = h.Counter.Count
   335	        res.Min = h.Counter.Min
   336	        res.Max = h.Counter.Max
   337	        res.Sum = h.Counter.Sum
   338	        res.Avg = h.Counter.Avg()
   339	        res.StdDev = h.Counter.StdDev()
   340	        multiplier := h.Divider
   341	        offset := h.Offset
   342	        // calculate the last bucket index
   343	        lastIdx := -1
   344	        for i := numBuckets - 1; i >= 0; i-- {
   345	                if h.Hdata[i] > 0 {
   346	                        lastIdx = i
   347	                        break
   348	                }
   349	        }
   350	        if lastIdx == -1 {
   351	                return &res
   352	        }
   353	
   354	        // previous bucket value:
   355	        prev := histogramBucketValues[0]
   356	        var total int64
   357	        ctrTotal := float64(h.Count)
   358	        // export the data of each bucket of the histogram
   359	        for i := 0; i <= lastIdx; i++ {
   360	                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
   361	                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
   362	                        if i < numValues {
   363	                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
   364	                        }
   365	                        continue
   366	                }
   367	                var b Bucket
   368	                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
   369	                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
   370	                        // First entry, start is min
   371	                        b.Start = h.Min
   372	                } else {
   373	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   374	                }
   375	                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
   376	                if i < numValues {
   377	                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
   378	                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
   379	                        prev = cur
   380	                } else {
   381	                        // Last Entry
   382	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   383	                        b.End = h.Max
   384	                }
   385	                b.Count = int64(h.Hdata[i])
   386	                res.Data = append(res.Data, b)
   387	        }
   388	        res.Data[len(res.Data)-1].End = h.Max
   389	        return &res
   390	}
   391	
   392	// CalcPercentiles calculates the requested percentile and adds them to the
   393	// HistogramData. Potential TODO: sort or assume sorting and calculate all
   394	// the percentiles in 1 pass (greater and greater values).
   395	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentiles(percentiles []float64) *HistogramData {
   396	        if e.Count == 0 {
   397	                return e
   398	        }
   399	        for _, p := range percentiles {
   400	                e.Percentiles = append(e.Percentiles, Percentile{p, e.CalcPercentile(p)})
   401	        }
   402	        return e
   403	}
   404	
   405	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   406	// Also calculates the percentile.
   407	func (e *HistogramData) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
   408	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   409	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : no data\n", msg)
   410	                return
   411	        }
   412	        // the base counterpart:
   413	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
   414	                msg, e.Count, e.Avg, e.StdDev, e.Min, e.Max, e.Sum)
   415	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintln(out, "# range, mid point, percentile, count")
   416	        sep := ">="
   417	        for i := range e.Data {
   418	                b := &e.Data[i]
   419	                if i > 0 {
   420	                        sep = ">" // last interval is inclusive (of max value)
   421	                }
   422	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s %.6g <= %.6g , %.6g , %.2f, %d\n", sep, b.Start, b.End, (b.Start+b.End)/2., b.Percent, b.Count)
   423	        }
   424	        // print the information of target percentiles
   425	        for _, p := range e.Percentiles {
   426	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "# target %g%% %.6g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
   427	        }
   428	}
   429	
   430	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   431	// Also calculates the percentiles. Use Export() once and Print if you
   432	// are going to need the Export results too.
   433	func (h *Histogram) Print(out io.Writer, msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   434	        h.Export().CalcPercentiles(percentiles).Print(out, msg)
   435	}
   436	
   437	// Log Logs the histogram to the counter.
   438	func (h *Histogram) Log(msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   439	        var b bytes.Buffer
   440	        w := bufio.NewWriter(&b)
   441	        h.Print(w, msg, percentiles)
   442	        _ = w.Flush()
   443	        log.Infof("%s", b.Bytes())
   444	}
   445	
   446	// Reset clears the data. Reset it to NewHistogram state.
   447	func (h *Histogram) Reset() {
   448	        h.Counter.Reset()
   449	        // Leave Offset and Divider alone
   450	        for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   451	                h.Hdata[i] = 0
   452	        }
   453	}
   454	
   455	// Clone returns a copy of the histogram.
   456	func (h *Histogram) Clone() *Histogram {
   457	        hCopy := NewHistogram(h.Offset, h.Divider)
   458	        hCopy.CopyFrom(h)
   459	        return hCopy
   460	}
   461	
   462	// CopyFrom sets the content of this object to a copy of the src.
   463	func (h *Histogram) CopyFrom(src *Histogram) {
   464	        h.Counter = src.Counter
   465	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   466	}
   467	
   468	// copyHDataFrom appends histogram data values to this object from the src.
   469	// Src histogram data values will be appended according to this object's
   470	// offset and divider.
   471	func (h *Histogram) copyHDataFrom(src *Histogram) {
   472	        if h.Divider == src.Divider && h.Offset == src.Offset {
   473	                for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   474	                        h.Hdata[i] += src.Hdata[i]
   475	                }
   476	                return
   477	        }
   478	        hData := src.Export()
   479	        for i := range hData.Data {
   480	                data := hData.Data[i]
   481	                h.record((data.Start+data.End)/2, int(data.Count))
   482	        }
   483	}
   484	
   485	// Merge two different histogram with different scale parameters
   486	// Lowest offset and highest divider value will be selected on new Histogram as scale parameters.
   487	func Merge(h1 *Histogram, h2 *Histogram) *Histogram {
   488	        divider := h1.Divider
   489	        offset := h1.Offset
   490	        if h2.Divider > h1.Divider {
   491	                divider = h2.Divider
   492	        }
   493	        if h2.Offset < h1.Offset {
   494	                offset = h2.Offset
   495	        }
   496	        newH := NewHistogram(offset, divider)
   497	        newH.Transfer(h1)
   498	        newH.Transfer(h2)
   499	        return newH
   500	}
   501	
   502	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Histogram and clears src.
   503	func (h *Histogram) Transfer(src *Histogram) {
   504	        if src.Count == 0 {
   505	                return
   506	        }
   507	        if h.Count == 0 {
   508	                h.CopyFrom(src)
   509	                src.Reset()
   510	                return
   511	        }
   512	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   513	        h.Counter.Transfer(&src.Counter)
   514	        src.Reset()
   515	}
   516	
   517	// ParsePercentiles extracts the percentiles from string (flag).
   518	func ParsePercentiles(percentiles string) ([]float64, error) {
   519	        percs := strings.Split(percentiles, ",") // will make a size 1 array for empty input!
   520	        res := make([]float64, 0, len(percs))
   521	        for _, pStr := range percs {
   522	                pStr = strings.TrimSpace(pStr)
   523	                if len(pStr) == 0 {
   524	                        continue
   525	                }
   526	                p, err := strconv.ParseFloat(pStr, 64)
   527	                if err != nil {
   528	                        return res, err
   529	                }
   530	                if p <= 0 || p >= 100 {
   531	                        return res, fmt.Errorf("percentile %g must be > 0 and < 100", p)
   532	                }
   533	                res = append(res, p)
   534	        }
   535	        if len(res) == 0 {
   536	                return res, errors.New("list can't be empty")
   537	        }
   538	        log.LogVf("Will use %v for percentiles", res)
   539	        return res, nil
   540	}

   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached
   328	}

   273	// Records v value to count times.
   274	func (h *Histogram) record(v float64, count int) {
   275	        // Scaled value to bucketize - we used to subtract epsilon because the interval
   276	        // is open to the left ] start, end ] so when exactly on start it has
   277	        // to fall on the previous bucket: which is more correctly done using
   278	        // math.Ceil()-1 but that doesn't work... so back to epsilon distance.
   279	        scaledVal := (v - h.Offset) / h.Divider
   280	        var idx int
   281	        switch {
   282	        case scaledVal <= firstValue:
   283	                idx = 0
   284	        case scaledVal > lastValue:
   285	                idx = numBuckets - 1 // last bucket is for > last value
   286	        default:
   287	                // else we look it up (with the open interval adjustment)
   288	                svInt := int(scaledVal)
   289	                delta := scaledVal - float64(svInt)
   290	                if delta < 1e-12 {
   291	                        svInt--
   292	                }
   293	                log.Debugf("v %f -> scaledVal %.17f ceil %f delta %g - svInt %d", v, scaledVal, math.Ceil(scaledVal), delta, svInt)
   294	                idx = lookUpIdx(svInt)
   295	        }
   296	        h.Hdata[idx] += int32(count) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   297	}

import json
import subprocess
import tempfile
import os
import sys

# Create a simple test to reproduce the issue
def test_histogram_with_low_resolution():
    # Create a test directory
    test_dir = tempfile.mkdtemp()
    
    # Create test data with all values around 0.5 seconds
    test_data = []
    for i in range(100):
        test_data.append(0.5)  # All values are 0.5 seconds
    
    # Test with different resolution values
    resolutions = [None, 0.0001, 0.00001, 0.000001]
    
    for resolution in resolutions:
        print(f"\n=== Testing with resolution: {resolution} ===")
        
        # Create histogram with test data
        test_file = os.path.join(test_dir, f"test_res_{resolution}.txt")
        with open(test_file, '"'"'w'"'"') as f:
            for value in test_data:
                f.write(f"{value}\n")
        
        # Run the histogram tool
        cmd = ['"'"'go'"'"', '"'"'run'"'"', '"'"'./histogram/main.go'"'"', '"'"'-json'"'"', '"'"'-p'"'"', '"'"'50,75,90,99,99.9'"'"']
        if resolution is not None:
            cmd.extend(['"'"'-offset'"'"', '"'"'0'"'"', '"'"'-divider'"'"', str(resolution)]
        
        cmd.append(test_file)
        
        try:
            result = subprocess.run(cmd, capture_output=True, text=True)
            if result.returncode == 0:
                data = json.loads(result.stdout)
                print(f"Count: {data['"'"'Count'"'"']}")
                print(f"Min: {data['"'"'Min'"'"']}")
                print(f"Max: {data['"'"'Max'"'"']}")
                print(f"Avg: {data['"'"'Avg'"'"']}")
                print("Percentiles:")
                for p in data['"'"'Percentiles'"'"']:
                    print(f"  {p['"'"'Percentile'"'"']}%: {p['"'"'Value'"'"']}")
                
                # Check if p50 is correct (should be close to 0.5)
                p50 = next(p['"'"'Value'"'"'] for p in data['"'"'Percentiles'"'"'] if p['"'"'Percentile'"'"'] == 50)
                if abs(p50 - 0.5) > 0.1:  # More than 100ms error
                    print(f"ERROR: p50 is {p50}, expected ~0.5")
                else:
                    print("p50 is correct")
            else:
                print(f"Error running command: {result.stderr}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Exception: {e}")
    
    # Cleanup
    import shutil
    shutil.rmtree(test_dir)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_histogram_with_low_resolution()'

    66	        expected += "test5" + finalExpected
    67	        // Try the Log() function too:
    68	        log.SetOutput(w)
    69	        log.SetFlags(0)
    70	        log.Config.LogFileAndLine = false
    71	        log.Config.LogPrefix = ""
    72	        c.Counter.Log("testLogC")
    73	        expected += "[I] testLogC" + finalExpected
    74	        _ = w.Flush()
    75	        actual := b.String()
    76	        if actual != expected {
    77	                t.Errorf("unexpected1:\n%s\nvs expected:\n%s\n", actual, expected)
    78	        }
    79	        b.Reset()
    80	        c.Log("testLogH", nil)
    81	        _ = w.Flush()
    82	        actual = b.String()
    83	        expected = "[I] testLogH" + finalExpected + `# range, mid point, percentile, count
    84	>= -977 <= 22 , -477.5 , 16.67, 1
    85	> 22.8 <= 22.9 , 22.85 , 50.00, 2
    86	> 23 <= 23.1 , 23.05 , 83.33, 2
    87	> 1022 <= 1023 , 1022.5 , 100.00, 1
    88	`
    89	        if actual != expected {
    90	                t.Errorf("unexpected2:\n%s\nvs expected:\n%s\n", actual, expected)
    91	        }
    92	        log.SetOutput(os.Stderr)
    93	}

    95	func TestTransferCounter(t *testing.T) {
    96	        var b bytes.Buffer
    97	        w := bufio.NewWriter(&b)
    98	        var c1 Counter
    99	        c1.Record(10)
   100	        c1.Record(20)
   101	        var c2 Counter
   102	        c2.Record(80)
   103	        c2.Record(90)
   104	        c1a := c1
   105	        c2a := c2
   106	        var c3 Counter
   107	        c1.Print(w, "c1 before merge")
   108	        c2.Print(w, "c2 before merge")
   109	        c1.Transfer(&c2)
   110	        c1.Print(w, "mergedC1C2")
   111	        c2.Print(w, "c2 after merge")
   112	        // reverse (exercise min if)
   113	        c2a.Transfer(&c1a)
   114	        c2a.Print(w, "mergedC2C1")
   115	        // test transfer into empty - min should be set
   116	        c3.Transfer(&c1)
   117	        c1.Print(w, "c1 should now be empty")
   118	        c3.Print(w, "c3 after merge - 1")
   119	        // test empty transfer - shouldn't reset min/no-op
   120	        c3.Transfer(&c2)
   121	        c3.Print(w, "c3 after merge - 2")
   122	        _ = w.Flush()
   123	        actual := b.String()
   124	        expected := `c1 before merge : count 2 avg 15 +/- 5 min 10 max 20 sum 30
   125	c2 before merge : count 2 avg 85 +/- 5 min 80 max 90 sum 170
   126	mergedC1C2 : count 4 avg 50 +/- 35.36 min 10 max 90 sum 200
   127	c2 after merge : count 0 avg 0 +/- 0 min 0 max 0 sum 0
   128	mergedC2C1 : count 4 avg 50 +/- 35.36 min 10 max 90 sum 200
   129	c1 should now be empty : count 0 avg 0 +/- 0 min 0 max 0 sum 0
   130	c3 after merge - 1 : count 4 avg 50 +/- 35.36 min 10 max 90 sum 200
   131	c3 after merge - 2 : count 4 avg 50 +/- 35.36 min 10 max 90 sum 200
   132	`
   133	        if actual != expected {
   134	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%s\tvs:\n%s", actual, expected)
   135	        }
   136	}

   145	func TestHistogram(t *testing.T) {
   146	        h := NewHistogram(0, 10)
   147	        h.Record(1)
   148	        h.Record(251)
   149	        h.Record(501)
   150	        h.Record(751)
   151	        h.Record(1001)
   152	        h.Print(os.Stdout, "TestHistogram", []float64{50})
   153	        e := h.Export()
   154	        for i := 25; i <= 100; i += 25 {
   155	                fmt.Printf("%d%% at %g\n", i, e.CalcPercentile(float64(i)))
   156	        }
   157	        tests := []struct {
   158	                actual   float64
   159	                expected float64
   160	                msg      string
   161	        }{
   162	                {h.Avg(), 501, "avg"},
   163	                {e.CalcPercentile(-1), 1, "p-1"}, // not valid but should return min
   164	                {e.CalcPercentile(0), 1, "p0"},
   165	                {e.CalcPercentile(0.1), 1, "p0.1"},
   166	                {e.CalcPercentile(1), 1, "p1"},
   167	                {e.CalcPercentile(20), 1, "p20"},             // 20% = first point, 1st bucket is 1-10
   168	                {e.CalcPercentile(20.01), 250.025, "p20.01"}, // near beginning of bucket of 2nd pt
   169	                {e.CalcPercentile(39.99), 299.975, "p39.99"},
   170	                {e.CalcPercentile(40), 300, "p40"},
   171	                {e.CalcPercentile(50), 550, "p50"},
   172	                {e.CalcPercentile(75), 775, "p75"},
   173	                {e.CalcPercentile(90), 1000.5, "p90"},
   174	                {e.CalcPercentile(99), 1000.95, "p99"},
   175	                {e.CalcPercentile(99.9), 1000.995, "p99.9"},
   176	                {e.CalcPercentile(100), 1001, "p100"},
   177	                {e.CalcPercentile(101), 1001, "p101"},
   178	        }
   179	        for _, tst := range tests {
   180	                if tst.actual != tst.expected {
   181	                        t.Errorf("%s: got %g, not as expected %g", tst.msg, tst.actual, tst.expected)
   182	                }
   183	        }
   184	}

   186	func TestPercentiles1(t *testing.T) {
   187	        h := NewHistogram(0, 10)
   188	        h.Record(10)
   189	        h.Record(20)
   190	        h.Record(30)
   191	        h.Print(os.Stdout, "TestPercentiles1", []float64{50})
   192	        e := h.Export()
   193	        for i := 0; i <= 100; i += 10 {
   194	                fmt.Printf("%d%% at %g\n", i, e.CalcPercentile(float64(i)))
   195	        }
   196	        tests := []struct {
   197	                actual   float64
   198	                expected float64
   199	                msg      string
   200	        }{
   201	                {h.Avg(), 20, "avg"},
   202	                {e.CalcPercentile(-1), 10, "p-1"}, // not valid but should return min
   203	                {e.CalcPercentile(0), 10, "p0"},
   204	                {e.CalcPercentile(0.1), 10, "p0.1"},
   205	                {e.CalcPercentile(1), 10, "p1"},
   206	                {e.CalcPercentile(20), 10, "p20"},           // 20% = first point, 1st bucket is 10
   207	                {e.CalcPercentile(33.33), 10, "p33.33"},     // near beginning of bucket of 2nd pt
   208	                {e.CalcPercentile(100 / 3), 10, "p100/3"},   // near beginning of bucket of 2nd pt
   209	                {e.CalcPercentile(33.34), 10.002, "p33.34"}, // near beginning of bucket of 2nd pt
   210	                {e.CalcPercentile(50), 15, "p50"},
   211	                {e.CalcPercentile(66.66), 19.998, "p66.66"},
   212	                {e.CalcPercentile(100. * 2 / 3), 20, "p100*2/3"},
   213	                {e.CalcPercentile(66.67), 20.001, "p66.67"},
   214	                {e.CalcPercentile(75), 22.5, "p75"},
   215	                {e.CalcPercentile(99), 29.7, "p99"},
   216	                {e.CalcPercentile(99.9), 29.97, "p99.9"},
   217	                {e.CalcPercentile(100), 30, "p100"},
   218	                {e.CalcPercentile(101), 30, "p101"},
   219	        }
   220	        for _, tst := range tests {
   221	                actualRounded := float64(int64(tst.actual*100000+0.5)) / 100000.
   222	                if actualRounded != tst.expected {
   223	                        t.Errorf("%s: got %g (%g), not as expected %g", tst.msg, actualRounded, tst.actual, tst.expected)
   224	                }
   225	        }
   226	}

   228	func TestHistogramData(t *testing.T) {
   229	        h := NewHistogram(0, 1)
   230	        h.Record(-1)
   231	        h.RecordN(0, 3)
   232	        h.Record(1)
   233	        h.Record(2)
   234	        h.Record(3)
   235	        h.Record(4)
   236	        h.RecordN(5, 2)
   237	        percs := []float64{0, 1, 10, 25, 40, 50, 60, 70, 80, 90, 99, 100}
   238	        e := h.Export().CalcPercentiles(percs)
   239	        e.Print(os.Stdout, "TestHistogramData")
   240	        assert.CheckEquals(t, int64(10), e.Count, "10 data points")
   241	        assert.CheckEquals(t, 1.9, e.Avg, "avg should be 2")
   242	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[0], Percentile{0, -1}, "p0 should be -1 (min)")
   243	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[1], Percentile{1, -1}, "p1 should be -1 (min)")
   244	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[2], Percentile{10, -1}, "p10 should be 1 (1/10 at min)")
   245	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[3], Percentile{25, -0.5}, "p25 should be half between -1 and 0")
   246	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[4], Percentile{40, 0}, "p40 should still be 0 (4/10 data pts at 0)")
   247	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[5], Percentile{50, 1}, "p50 should 1 (5th/10 point is 1)")
   248	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[6], Percentile{60, 2}, "p60 should 2 (6th/10 point is 2)")
   249	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[7], Percentile{70, 3}, "p70 should 3 (7th/10 point is 3)")
   250	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[8], Percentile{80, 4}, "p80 should 4 (8th/10 point is 4)")
   251	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[9], Percentile{90, 4.5}, "p90 should between 4 and 5 (2 points in bucket)")
   252	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[10], Percentile{99, 4.95}, "p99")
   253	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[11], Percentile{100, 5}, "p100 should 5 (10th/10 point is 5 and max is 5)")
   254	        h.Log("test multi count", percs)
   255	}
   256	
   257	// Checks properties that should be true for all non-empty histograms.
   258	func CheckGenericHistogramDataProperties(t *testing.T, e *HistogramData) {
   259	        n := len(e.Data)
   260	        if n <= 0 {
   261	                t.Error("Unexpected empty histogram")
   262	
   263	                return
   264	        }
   265	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Data[0].Start, e.Min, "first bucket starts at min")
   266	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Data[n-1].End, e.Max, "end of last bucket is max")
   267	        assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Data[n-1].Percent, 100., "last bucket is 100%")
   268	        // All buckets in order
   269	        var prev Bucket
   270	        var sum int64
   271	        for i := range n {
   272	                b := e.Data[i]
   273	                assert.Assert(t, b.Start <= b.End, "End %f should always be after Start %f", b.End, b.Start)
   274	                assert.Assert(t, b.Count > 0, "Every exported bucket should have data")
   275	                assert.Assert(t, b.Percent > 0, "Percentage should always be positive")
   276	                sum += b.Count
   277	                if i > 0 {
   278	                        assert.Assert(t, b.Start >= prev.End, "Start of next bucket >= end of previous")
   279	                        assert.Assert(t, b.Percent > prev.Percent, "Percentage should be ever increasing")
   280	                }
   281	                prev = b
   282	        }
   283	        assert.CheckEquals(t, sum, e.Count, "Sum in buckets should add up to Counter's count")
   284	}

   375	func TestHistogramExportRandom(t *testing.T) {
   376	        seed := time.Now().UnixNano()
   377	        r := rand.New(rand.NewSource(seed))
   378	        for i := range NumRandomHistogram {
   379	                // offset [-500,500[  divisor ]0,100]
   380	                offset := (r.Float64() - 0.5) * 1000
   381	                div := 100 * (1 - r.Float64())
   382	                numEntries := 1 + r.Int31n(10000)
   383	                // fmt.Printf("new histogram with offset %g, div %g - will insert %d entries\n", offset, div, numEntries)
   384	                h := NewHistogram(offset, div)
   385	                var n int32
   386	                var minV float64
   387	                var maxV float64
   388	                for ; n < numEntries; n++ {
   389	                        v := 3000 * (r.Float64() - 0.25)
   390	                        if n == 0 {
   391	                                minV = v
   392	                                maxV = v
   393	                        } else {
   394	                                if v < minV {
   395	                                        minV = v
   396	                                } else if v > maxV {
   397	                                        maxV = v
   398	                                }
   399	                        }
   400	                        h.Record(v)
   401	                }
   402	                e := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{0, 50, 100})
   403	                CheckGenericHistogramDataProperties(t, e)
   404	                assert.CheckEquals(t, h.Count, int64(numEntries), "num entries should match")
   405	                assert.CheckEquals(t, h.Min, minV, "Min should match")
   406	                assert.CheckEquals(t, h.Max, maxV, "Max should match")
   407	                assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[0].Value, minV, "p0 should be min")
   408	                assert.CheckEquals(t, e.Percentiles[2].Value, maxV, "p100 should be max")
   409	                if t.Failed() {
   410	                        t.Logf("Failed seed %v iter %d, offset %v, div %v, numEntries %v", seed, i, offset, div, numEntries)
   411	                        t.Logf("%v", e)
   412	                        t.FailNow()
   413	                }
   414	        }
   415	}

   417	func TestHistogramLastBucket(t *testing.T) {
   418	        // Use -1 offset, so first bucket is negative values
   419	        h := NewHistogram( /* offset */ -1 /*scale */, 1)

   473	func TestMergeHistogramsWithDifferentScales(t *testing.T) {
   474	        tP := []float64{100.}
   475	        var b bytes.Buffer
   476	        w := bufio.NewWriter(&b)
   477	        h1 := NewHistogram(0, 10)
   478	        h1.Record(20)
   479	        h1.Record(50)
   480	        h1.Record(90)
   481	        h2 := NewHistogram(2, 100)
   482	        h2.Record(30)
   483	        h2.Record(40)
   484	        h2.Record(50)
   485	        newH := Merge(h1, h2)
   486	        newH.Print(w, "h1 and h2 merged", tP)
   487	        w.Flush()
   488	        actual := b.String()
   489	        expected := `h1 and h2 merged : count 6 avg 46.666667 +/- 22.11 min 20 max 90 sum 280
   490	# range, mid point, percentile, count
   491	>= 20 <= 90 , 55 , 100.00, 6
   492	# target 100% 90
   493	`
   494	        if newH.Divider != h2.Divider {
   495	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%f\tvs:\n%f", newH.Divider, h2.Divider)
   496	        }
   497	        if newH.Offset != h1.Offset {
   498	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%f\tvs:\n%f", newH.Offset, h1.Offset)
   499	        }
   500	        if actual != expected {
   501	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%s\tvs:\n%s", actual, expected)
   502	        }
   503	
   504	        b.Reset()
   505	        h3 := NewHistogram(5, 200)
   506	        h3.Record(10000)
   507	        h3.Record(5000)
   508	        h3.Record(9000)
   509	        h4 := NewHistogram(2, 100)
   510	        h4.Record(300)
   511	        h4.Record(400)
   512	        h4.Record(50)
   513	        newH = Merge(h3, h4)
   514	        newH.Print(w, "h3 and h4 merged", tP)
   515	        w.Flush()
   516	        actual = b.String()
   517	        expected = `h3 and h4 merged : count 6 avg 4125 +/- 4167 min 50 max 10000 sum 24750
   518	# range, mid point, percentile, count
   519	>= 50 <= 202 , 126 , 16.67, 1
   520	> 202 <= 402 , 302 , 50.00, 2
   521	> 5002 <= 6002 , 5502 , 66.67, 1
   522	> 8002 <= 9002 , 8502 , 83.33, 1
   523	> 9002 <= 10000 , 9501 , 100.00, 1
   524	# target 100% 10000
   525	`
   526	        if newH.Divider != h3.Divider {
   527	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%f\tvs:\n%f", newH.Divider, h3.Divider)
   528	        }
   529	        if newH.Offset != h4.Offset {
   530	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%f\tvs:\n%f", newH.Offset, h4.Offset)
   531	        }
   532	        if actual != expected {
   533	                t.Errorf("unexpected:\n%s\tvs:\n%s", actual, expected)
   534	        }
   535	}

   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached

import json
import subprocess
import tempfile
import os

# Create a simple test to debug the issue
def debug_histogram_with_low_resolution():
    # Create a test directory
    test_dir = tempfile.mkdtemp()
    
    # Create test data with all values around 0.5 seconds
    test_data = []
    for i in range(100):
        test_data.append(0.5)  # All values are 0.5 seconds
    
    # Test with the problematic resolution
    resolution = 0.000001
    
    print(f"\n=== Testing with resolution: {resolution} ===")
    
    # Create histogram with test data
    test_file = os.path.join(test_dir, "test_data.txt")
    with open(test_file, '"'"'w'"'"') as f:
        for value in test_data:
            f.write(f"{value}\n")
    
    # Run the histogram tool
    cmd = ['"'"'./histogram/histo'"'"', '"'"'-json'"'"', '"'"'-p'"'"', '"'"'50,75,90,99,99.9'"'"', '"'"'-offset'"'"', '"'"'0'"'"', '"'"'-divider'"'"', str(resolution)]
    
    try:
        with open(test_file, '"'"'r'"'"') as input_file:
            result = subprocess.run(cmd, stdin=input_file, capture_output=True, text=True)
        if result.returncode == 0:
            data = json.loads(result.stdout)
            print(f"Count: {data['"'"'Count'"'"']}")
            print(f"Min: {data['"'"'Min'"'"']}")
            print(f"Max: {data['"'"'Max'"'"']}")

Now I understand the issue! The problem is in the `Export()` function. When all data points fall into a single bucket (which happens with very low resolution values), the bucket creation logic is incorrect.

Let me trace through what happens:

1. With resolution = 0.000001 (divider = 1e-06), the scaled value becomes `(0.5 - 0) / 1e-06 = 500000`
2. This value is larger than `lastValue` (which is 100000), so it goes into the last bucket (index = numBuckets - 1)
3. In the `Export()` function, when processing this bucket:
   - Since it's the last bucket (i >= numValues), it uses the logic at lines 381-384
   - `b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset` where `multiplier = divider = 1e-06` and `prev` is the last value from the previous iteration
   - `b.End = h.Max` which is 0.5

The issue is that when all data points are in the last bucket, the `prev` value might not be correctly set, leading to an incorrect `b.Start` value. In our case, `b.Start` is set to 0.09999999999999999 instead of the correct value.

Let me check what `prev` should be in this case by looking at the histogram bucket values:

str_replace_editor create /testbed/trace_calculation.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func main() {
	resolution := 0.000001
	offset := 0.0
	
	h := stats.NewHistogram(offset, resolution)
	
	// Record 100 values of 0.5 seconds
	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		h.Record(0.5)
	}
	
	// Export the data
	exported := h.Export()
	
	fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", exported.Count)
	fmt.Printf("Min: %f\n", exported.Min)
	fmt.Printf("Max: %f\n", exported.Max)
	fmt.Printf("Avg: %f\n", exported.Avg)
	
	fmt.Printf("\nBucket Data:\n")
	for i, bucket := range exported.Data {
		fmt.Printf("  Bucket %d: Start=%f, End=%f, Percent=%f, Count=%d\n", 
			i, bucket.Start, bucket.End, bucket.Percent, bucket.Count)
	}
	
	// Calculate percentiles
	percentiles := []float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9}
	exported.CalcPercentiles(percentiles)
	
	fmt.Printf("\nPercentiles:\n")
	for _, p := range exported.Percentiles {
		fmt.Printf("  %.1f%%: %f\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
	}
	
	// Debug: Let'"'"'s understand what bucket the value 0.5 falls into
	scaledVal := (0.5 - offset) / resolution
	fmt.Printf("\nDebug: scaledVal = %f\n", scaledVal)
	fmt.Printf("firstValue = %f\n", 0.0)
	fmt.Printf("lastValue = %f\n", 100000.0)
}'

2026-01-08 16:49:05,981 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I see the issue now. Let me analyze what's happening in the code more systematically.

The problem is in the `Export()` function in `/testbed/stats/stats.go`. When all data points fall into a single bucket (which happens with very low resolution values), the bucket creation logic is incorrect.

Let me trace through the logic:

1. With resolution = 0.000001 (divider = 1e-06), the scaled value becomes `(0.5 - 0) / 1e-06 = 500000`
2. This value is larger than `lastValue` (which is 100000), so it goes into the last bucket (index = numBuckets - 1)
3. In the `Export()` function, when processing this bucket:
   - Since it's the last bucket (i >= numValues), it uses the logic at lines 381-384
   - `b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset` where `multiplier = divider = 1e-06` and `prev` is the last value from the previous iteration
   - `b.End = h.Max` which is 0.5

The issue is that when all data points are in the last bucket, the `prev` value might not be correctly set, leading to an incorrect `b.Start` value. In our case, `b.Start` is set to 0.09999999999999999 instead of the correct value.

Let me examine the specific issue in the `Export()` function:

str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_issue.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func main() {
	// Test different resolution values
	resolutions := []float64{0.001, 0.0001, 0.00001, 0.000001}
	
	for _, resolution := range resolutions {
		fmt.Printf("\n=== Testing with resolution: %v ===\n", resolution)
		
		h := stats.NewHistogram(0, resolution)
		
		// Record 100 values of 0.5 seconds
		for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
			h.Record(0.5)
		}
		
		// Export and calculate percentiles
		exported := h.Export()
		percentiles := []float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9}
		exported.CalcPercentiles(percentiles)
		
		fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", exported.Count)
		fmt.Printf("Min: %f\n", exported.Min)
		fmt.Printf("Max: %f\n", exported.Max)
		fmt.Printf("Avg: %f\n", exported.Avg)
		
		fmt.Printf("Bucket Data count: %d\n", len(exported.Data))
		if len(exported.Data) > 0 {
			fmt.Printf("First bucket: Start=%f, End=%f, Percent=%f, Count=%d\n",
				exported.Data[0].Start, exported.Data[0].End, exported.Data[0].Percent, exported.Data[0].Count)
		}
		
		fmt.Printf("Percentiles:\n")
		for _, p := range exported.Percentiles {
			fmt.Printf("  %.1f%%: %f\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
		}
		
		// Check p50
		p50 := exported.CalcPercentile(50)
		if p50 < 0.4 || p50 > 0.6 {
			fmt.Printf("ERROR: p50 is %f, expected ~0.5\n", p50)
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("p50 is correct\n")
		}
	}
}'

   273	// Records v value to count times.
   274	func (h *Histogram) record(v float64, count int) {
   275	        // Scaled value to bucketize - we used to subtract epsilon because the interval
   276	        // is open to the left ] start, end ] so when exactly on start it has
   277	        // to fall on the previous bucket: which is more correctly done using
   278	        // math.Ceil()-1 but that doesn't work... so back to epsilon distance.
   279	        scaledVal := (v - h.Offset) / h.Divider
   280	        var idx int
   281	        switch {
   282	        case scaledVal <= firstValue:
   283	                idx = 0
   284	        case scaledVal > lastValue:
   285	                idx = numBuckets - 1 // last bucket is for > last value
   286	        default:
   287	                // else we look it up (with the open interval adjustment)
   288	                svInt := int(scaledVal)
   289	                delta := scaledVal - float64(svInt)
   290	                if delta < 1e-12 {
   291	                        svInt--
   292	                }
   293	                log.Debugf("v %f -> scaledVal %.17f ceil %f delta %g - svInt %d", v, scaledVal, math.Ceil(scaledVal), delta, svInt)
   294	                idx = lookUpIdx(svInt)
   295	        }
   296	        h.Hdata[idx] += int32(count) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   297	}

2026-01-08 16:51:07,140 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue! Let me analyze the problem step by step:

1. **The Issue**: When all data points fall into the last bucket (which happens with very low resolution values), the bucket start value is incorrectly calculated.

2. **Root Cause**: In the `Export()` function, when processing the last bucket (`i >= numValues`), the start value is calculated as `multiplier*float64(prev) + offset`. However, `prev` is not being correctly updated when the only data is in the last bucket.

3. **What's happening with resolution = 0.000001**:
   - `scaledVal = 0.5 / 0.000001 = 500000`
   - Since `500000 > 100000`, it goes into the last bucket (index = numBuckets - 1)
   - In the `Export()` function, when processing this bucket:
     - `prev` starts as `histogramBucketValues[0] = 0`
     - The loop encounters empty buckets first and updates `prev` through line 363
     - Eventually, it reaches the last bucket and sets `b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset`
     - But `prev` might be an intermediate value from the empty bucket processing, not the actual start of the bucket

The fix is to ensure that when all data points are in a single bucket (especially the last bucket), the bucket boundaries are correctly calculated. In this case, since all data points are exactly the same value (0.5), the bucket should have `Start = 0.5` and `End = 0.5`.

Let me implement the fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/stats/stats.go   --old_str '        // export the data of each bucket of the histogram
        for i := 0; i <= lastIdx; i++ {
                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
                        if i < numValues {
                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
                        }
                        continue
                }
                var b Bucket
                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
                        // First entry, start is min
                        b.Start = h.Min
                } else {
                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
                }
                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
                if i < numValues {
                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
                        prev = cur
                } else {
                        // Last Entry
                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
                        b.End = h.Max
                }
                b.Count = int64(h.Hdata[i])
                res.Data = append(res.Data, b)

        for i := 0; i <= lastIdx; i++ {
                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
                        if i < numValues {
                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
                        }
                        continue
                }
                var b Bucket
                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
                        // First entry, start is min
                        b.Start = h.Min
                } else {
                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
                }
                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
                if i < numValues {
                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
                        prev = cur
                } else {
                        // Last Entry
                        // If we have only one bucket and it'"'"'s the last one, and all values are the same,
                        // then the bucket boundaries should be [min, max] instead of [prev, max]
                        if len(res.Data) == 0 && h.Min == h.Max {
                                b.Start = h.Min
                        } else {
                                b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset

                        b.End = h.Max

   360	                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
   361	                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
   362	                        if i < numValues {
   363	                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
   364	                        }
   365	                        continue
   366	                }
   367	                var b Bucket
   368	                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
   369	                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
   370	                        // First entry, start is min
   371	                        b.Start = h.Min
   372	                } else {
   373	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   374	                }
   375	                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
   376	                if i < numValues {
   377	                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
   378	                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
   379	                        prev = cur
   380	                } else {
   381	                        // Last Entry
   382	                        // If we have only one bucket and it's the last one, and all values are the same,
   383	                        // then the bucket boundaries should be [min, max] instead of [prev, max]
   384	                        if len(res.Data) == 0 && h.Min == h.Max {
   385	                                b.Start = h.Min
   386	                        } else {
   387	                                b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   388	                        }
   389	                        b.End = h.Max
   390	                }
   391	                b.Count = int64(h.Hdata[i])
   392	                res.Data = append(res.Data, b)
   393	        }
   394	        res.Data[len(res.Data)-1].End = h.Max
   395	        return &res
   396	}
Review the changes and make sure they are as expected. Edit the file again if necessary.

import (
	"fmt"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func testCase(name string, values []float64, resolution float64) {
	fmt.Printf("\n=== Test Case: %s ===\n", name)
	
	h := stats.NewHistogram(0, resolution)
	
	for _, v := range values {
		h.Record(v)
	}
	
	// Export and calculate percentiles
	exported := h.Export()
	percentiles := []float64{50}
	exported.CalcPercentiles(percentiles)
	
	fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", exported.Count)
	fmt.Printf("Min: %f\n", exported.Min)
	fmt.Printf("Max: %f\n", exported.Max)
	fmt.Printf("Avg: %f\n", exported.Avg)
	
	fmt.Printf("Bucket Data count: %d\n", len(exported.Data))
	for i, bucket := range exported.Data {
		fmt.Printf("  Bucket %d: Start=%f, End=%f, Percent=%f, Count=%d\n",
			i, bucket.Start, bucket.End, bucket.Percent, bucket.Count)
	}
	
	p50 := exported.CalcPercentile(50)
	expectedMin := exported.Min
	expectedMax := exported.Max
	
	if p50 < expectedMin || p50 > expectedMax {
		fmt.Printf("ERROR: p50 is %f, should be between %f and %f\n", p50, expectedMin, expectedMax)
	} else if len(values) == 1 && exported.Min == exported.Max && exported.Max != p50 {
		fmt.Printf("ERROR: p50 is %f, should be %f since all values are the same\n", p50, exported.Max)
	} else {
		fmt.Printf("p50 is correct: %f\n", p50)
	}
}

func main() {
	// Test case 1: All values same with low resolution
	testCase("All same values, resolution 1e-6", []float64{0.5, 0.5, 0.5}, 0.000001)
	
	// Test case 2: Different values with low resolution  
	testCase("Different values, resolution 1e-6", []float64{0.4, 0.5, 0.6}, 0.000001)
	
	// Test case 3: Single value with low resolution
	testCase("Single value, resolution 1e-6", []float64{0.5}, 0.000001)
	
	// Test case 4: All same values with default resolution
	testCase("All same values, resolution 0.001", []float64{0.5, 0.5, 0.5}, 0.001)
	
	// Test case 5: Edge case where min != max but all values might fall in single bucket
	testCase("Very close values, resolution 1e-6", []float64{0.500001, 0.500001, 0.500001}, 0.000001)
	
	// Test case 6: Normal case with medium resolution
	testCase("Normal distribution, resolution 0.001", []float64{0.4, 0.45, 0.5, 0.55, 0.6}, 0.001)
}'

   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached
   328	}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_pr_scenario.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func main() {
	// Reproduce the exact scenario from the PR description
	h := stats.NewHistogram(0, 0.000001) // -r 0.000001
	
	// Record 100 values of ~500ms (similar to what fortio load would do)
	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		// Values around 0.5 seconds
		h.Record(0.501253173)
		h.Record(0.502924856)
	}
	
	// Export and calculate percentiles like fortio would
	exported := h.Export()
	percentiles := []float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9}
	exported.CalcPercentiles(percentiles)
	
	// Print results in similar format to the PR description
	fmt.Printf("{\n")
	fmt.Printf("  \"Count\": %d,\n", exported.Count)
	fmt.Printf("  \"Min\": %g,\n", exported.Min)
	fmt.Printf("  \"Max\": %g,\n", exported.Max)
	fmt.Printf("  \"Sum\": %g,\n", exported.Sum)
	fmt.Printf("  \"Avg\": %g,\n", exported.Avg)
	fmt.Printf("  \"StdDev\": %g,\n", exported.StdDev)
	
	fmt.Printf("  \"Data\": [\n")
	for i, bucket := range exported.Data {
		fmt.Printf("    {\n")
		fmt.Printf("      \"Start\": %g,\n", bucket.Start)
		fmt.Printf("      \"End\": %g,\n", bucket.End)
		fmt.Printf("      \"Percent\": %g,\n", bucket.Percent)
		fmt.Printf("      \"Count\": %d\n", bucket.Count)
		if i < len(exported.Data)-1 {
			fmt.Printf("    },\n")
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("    }\n")
		}
	}
	fmt.Printf("  ],\n")
	
	fmt.Printf("  \"Percentiles\": [\n")
	for i, p := range exported.Percentiles {
		fmt.Printf("    {\n")
		fmt.Printf("      \"Percentile\": %g,\n", p.Percentile)
		fmt.Printf("      \"Value\": %g\n", p.Value)
		if i < len(exported.Percentiles)-1 {
			fmt.Printf("    },\n")
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("    }\n")
		}
	}
	fmt.Printf("  ]\n")
	fmt.Printf("}\n")

	// Validate that p50 is ~500ms (around 0.5)
	p50 := exported.CalcPercentile(50)
	if p50 > 0.4 && p50 < 0.6 {
		fmt.Printf("\nPASS: p50 is %g (approximately 500ms as expected)\n", p50)
	} else {
		fmt.Printf("\nFAIL: p50 is %g (expected ~0.5)\n", p50)
	}
}'

I have successfully implemented the fix for the histogram bucketing issue with low resolution values. The problem has been resolved by modifying the `Export()` method in `/testbed/stats/stats.go` to correctly set bucket boundaries when all data points fall into a single bucket.

The fix ensures that when there's only one bucket containing all the data, the bucket boundaries are set to the actual `Min` and `Max` values of the data instead of the incorrectly calculated scaled boundaries. This prevents incorrect percentile calculations like the p50 showing as ~299ms instead of the correct ~500ms when using very low resolution values like `-r 0.000001`.

All tests pass and the specific scenario described in the PR is now working correctly.

+                // If there will be no more buckets, and we have only one bucket,
+                // ensure the bucket boundaries reflect the actual data range
+                if i == lastIdx && len(res.Data) == 1 {
+                        // Single bucket case - use actual min/max as boundaries
+                        res.Data[0].Start = h.Min
+                        res.Data[0].End = h.Max
+                }
+        }
+        res.Data[len(res.Data)-1].End = h.Max
+        return &res
 }
